Dear Bess,
 
Having just won a Laocoon-like struggle to change
 
the ribbon on my antique old Underwood, I can now res ond
 
to your a& welcome letter.
 
First of all, do, Do  DO call when you're in LA
 
in Aprilt  The number is
 l) 44
.9-70 9.
 
Sorry to hear about your flu  (
don't you get amt
h
 
an annual flu shot?) and all your hos ital tests, but
 
delighted to hear that they worked out "nicely."  I
've
 
had a similar set of experiences.
 
January was made hideous by modern medicine.  Marty
 
Shickman, that painfully cons ±entious fellow, called me
 
in for my usual three-month morale and blood pressure
 
check-up and heard lots of rumbling and gurgling in my
 
abdomen.  I said it must have been something I ate, but
 
he pressed the panic button; first, a gastroenterologist
 
prowling around my colon with one of these new flexible
 
sigmoidoscopes that seem to go from rump to tonsils (
net
 
discovery was one small benign polyp); second, third, and
 
fourth, the whole GI radiology series, with lots of barium,
 
compressed air and before and after laxatiges (
all this
 
abuse of the G
I track found nothing, but it certainly
 
made the rumbling and the gurgling go awayñi.  Marty,
 
very happy with himself, said that he now had peace of
 
mind; I
, much less happy, wished that he had found peach
 
through transcendental meditation.
 
A little later, in February, I was opening my morning
 
ma l
l and suddenly had chest pains.  After about ten minutes
 
of wondering whether this was more GI nonsense, I remembered
 
that Marty frequently insists that self-diagnosis is stupid
 
and frequently suicidal, so I called paramedics and roared
 
off to Huntington Memorial Hospital, siren wailing and
 
lights flashing while pains were subsiding.
 
The hospital took EKG's, along with the usual chest
 
X-ray and enoughblood to feed all the vampires in their
 
basement; then they checked by telert
hone with Marty and
 
reported that there had been a change in the EKG.  So I
 
was put in the Coronary Care Unit, all wired and tubed
 
and IV'd and restrained.  The N next day, however, the
 
heart enzymes and EKG were normal, and I was said to have
 
had a transitory ischemic attack with no heart damage.  So,
 
in on Tuesday and out on Friday.
 
2
 
For Marty, of course, this was a whole new oyportunity
 
to summon all the resources of modern medicine.  First, his
 
own EKG and blood workup; then, an exam by a cardiologist
 
with space-age equipment; then, finally, into UCLA for
 
three days for a heart catheterization (
angiogram) that
 
showed no additional damage since the heart attack five
 
years ago.  So now I have a clean bill of health and a
 
strong desi±e to take up Christian Science.
 
Now I
'm struggling with my inadequate financial
 
records for 1985
, a year in which I sold a house and
 
reached an age that made me terminate a Keough account
 
and draw on an IRA.  I hope John Lamb can make some
 
not too painful sense of all this next week.
 
Then, bless my much examined heart, I plan to leave
 
for England only a few days after seeing you (you will
 
cailt), and I
'll probably spend a self-indulgent month
 
to six weeks;there and on the continent.
 
Pam and George (who would also like to se(  you) and
 
all i
three grandchildren are well and terribly busy.  We
 
have, incidentally, an empty guest room if you can use it.
 
On any travel arrangements we might make, if ever
 
you selfishly get some leisure (
Can't Federal employees
 
take leave without pay for physical or psychological
 
health?  That way, you wouldn't make the Endowment lose
 
the position.), you'd probably never or rarely w nt to
 
hear my snores in a room on land.  Except in peak seasons
 
in resorts, Itve become expert at nosing out reasonable
 
single rooms.  It's when you consider cabins or stn terooms
 
on ships, boats, or barges that the charge for singles
 
becomes outrageous.
 
Then I'm in England, I'll check out charges and
 
programs.  Floating Through  Europe looks like fun, but
 
any trip that begins and ends in Paris at the Plaza
 
Athenee (only slightly more expensive than the Ritz)
 
is not going to be cheap.  However, sometimes extravagange
 
is fun,  the Beverly & Jean in Shakespeare Country runs
 
only to Hiltons, and so is slightly more modest.  I would
 
myself skip all the Stratford cottages; actually their
 
whole program seems to involve a h'* lot of touring on
 
buses and not much mileage on the  Severn and Avon.
 
But enough carping.  I'll do wome serious research.
 
I enclose a clipiing.  And I DO want to see you
 
All the best to you, to Corey, and to Mike,
